# GitHub CLI Repository Summary

This is the official GitHub CLI tool repository (`cli/cli`), a command-line interface that integrates GitHub functionality directly into your terminal workflow.

## Key Information

**Project Description:**
"gh is GitHub on the command line. It brings pull requests, issues, and other GitHub concepts to the terminal next to where you are already working with git and your code."

**Repository Stats:**
- 42.8k stars
- 8k forks
- 10,824 commits
- 590 contributors
- Written in Go (99.2%)

## Installation Options

The tool supports multiple installation methods:
- **macOS:** Homebrew or precompiled binaries
- **Linux/Unix:** Debian, RPM-based systems, or binaries
- **Windows:** WinGet or precompiled binaries
- **From source:** Available via documentation
- **GitHub Codespaces & Actions:** Pre-configured support

## Platform Support

GitHub CLI works with GitHub.com, GitHub Enterprise Cloud, and GitHub Enterprise Server 2.20+, across macOS, Windows, and Linux.

## Notable Features

- Binary verification using Sigstore attestations (v2.50.0+)
- Comprehensive documentation at cli.github.com
- Active contribution guidelines in the repository

The latest release is version 2.87.3 (February 23, 2026).

     1→import type { ComposerTranslation } from 'vue-i18n'
     2→import type { $ZodType } from 'zod/v4/core'
     3→
     4→import type { ProviderDefinition } from '../types'
     5→
     6→import { orderBy } from 'es-toolkit'
     7→
     8→const providerRegistry = new Map<string, ProviderDefinition>()
     9→
    10→export function listProviders(): ProviderDefinition[] {
    11→  const providerDefs = Array.from(providerRegistry.values()).map(def => ({ order: 99999, ...def }))
    12→  const sorted = orderBy(providerDefs, [p => p.order, 'name'], ['asc', 'asc'])
    13→  return sorted
    14→}
    15→
    16→export function getDefinedProvider(id: string): ProviderDefinition | undefined {
    17→  return providerRegistry.get(id)
    18→}
    19→
    20→export function defineProvider<T>(definition: { createProviderConfig: (contextOptions: { t: ComposerTranslation }) => $ZodType<T> } & ProviderDefinition<T>): ProviderDefinition<T> {
    21→  const provider = {
    22→    ...definition,
    23→  }
    24→
    25→  providerRegistry.set(definition.id, definition)
    26→
    27→  return provider
    28→}

     1→<script setup lang="ts">
     2→import type { RemovableRef } from '@vueuse/core'
     3→
     4→import {
     5→  Alert,
     6→  ProviderAdvancedSettings,
     7→  ProviderBaseUrlInput,
     8→  ProviderBasicSettings,
     9→  ProviderSettingsContainer,
    10→  ProviderSettingsLayout,
    11→} from '@proj-airi/stage-ui/components'
    12→import { useProviderValidation } from '@proj-airi/stage-ui/composables/use-provider-validation'
    13→import { useProvidersStore } from '@proj-airi/stage-ui/stores/providers'
    14→import { FieldKeyValues } from '@proj-airi/ui'
    15→import { storeToRefs } from 'pinia'
    16→import { computed, onMounted, ref, watch } from 'vue'
    17→
    18→const providerId = 'ollama'
    19→const providersStore = useProvidersStore()
    20→const { providers } = storeToRefs(providersStore) as { providers: RemovableRef<Record<string, any>> }
    21→
    22→// Define computed properties for credentials
    23→const baseUrl = computed({
    24→  get: () => providers.value[providerId]?.baseUrl || 'http://localhost:11434/v1/',
    25→  set: (value) => {
    26→    if (!providers.value[providerId])
    27→      providers.value[providerId] = {}
    28→    providers.value[providerId].baseUrl = value
    29→  },
    30→})
    31→
    32→// Use the composable to get validation logic and state
    33→const {
    34→  t,
    35→  router,
    36→  providerMetadata,
    37→  isValidating,
    38→  isValid,
    39→  validationMessage,
    40→  handleResetSettings,
    41→  forceValid,
    42→} = useProviderValidation(providerId)
    43→
    44→const headers = ref<{ key: string, value: string }[]>(Object.entries(providers.value[providerId]?.headers || {}).map(([key, value]) => ({ key, value } as { key: string, value: string })) || [{ key: '', value: '' }])
    45→
    46→function addKeyValue(headers: { key: string, value: string }[], key: string, value: string) {
    47→  if (!headers)
    48→    return
    49→
    50→  headers.push({ key, value })
    51→}
    52→
    53→function removeKeyValue(index: number, headers: { key: string, value: string }[]) {
    54→  if (!headers)
    55→    return
    56→
    57→  if (headers.length === 1) {
    58→    headers[0].key = ''
    59→    headers[0].value = ''
    60→  }
    61→  else {
    62→    headers.splice(index, 1)
    63→  }
    64→}
    65→
    66→watch(headers, (headers) => {
    67→  if (headers.length > 0 && (headers[headers.length - 1].key !== '' || headers[headers.length - 1].value !== '')) {
    68→    headers.push({ key: '', value: '' })
    69→  }
    70→  if (!providers.value[providerId])
    71→    return
    72→  providers.value[providerId].headers = headers.filter(header => header.key !== '').reduce((acc, header) => {
    73→    acc[header.key] = header.value
    74→    return acc
    75→  }, {} as Record<string, string>)
    76→}, {
    77→  deep: true,
    78→  immediate: true,
    79→})
    80→
    81→async function refetch() {
    82→  try {
    83→    const validationResult = await providerMetadata.value.validators.validateProviderConfig({
    84→      baseUrl: baseUrl.value,
    85→      headers: headers.value.filter(header => header.key !== '').reduce((acc, header) => {
    86→        acc[header.key] = header.value
    87→        return acc
    88→      }, {} as Record<string, string>),
    89→    })
    90→
    91→    if (!validationResult.valid) {
    92→      validationMessage.value = t('settings.dialogs.onboarding.validationError', {
    93→        error: validationResult.reason,
    94→      })
    95→    }
    96→  }
    97→  catch (error) {
    98→    validationMessage.value = t('settings.dialogs.onboarding.validationError', {
    99→      error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error),
   100→    })
   101→  }
   102→}
   103→
   104→watch([baseUrl, headers], refetch, { immediate: true })
   105→watch(headers, refetch, { deep: true })
   106→
   107→onMounted(() => {
   108→  providersStore.initializeProvider(providerId)
   109→
   110→  // Initialize refs with current values
   111→  baseUrl.value = providers.value[providerId]?.baseUrl || providerMetadata.value?.defaultOptions?.().baseUrl || ''
   112→
   113→  // Initialize headers if not already set
   114→  if (!providers.value[providerId]?.headers) {
   115→    providers.value[providerId].headers = {}
   116→  }
   117→  if (headers.value.length === 0) {
   118→    headers.value = [{ key: '', value: '' }]
   119→  }
   120→})
   121→</script>
   122→
   123→<template>
   124→  <ProviderSettingsLayout
   125→    :provider-name="providerMetadata?.localizedName"
   126→    :provider-icon-color="providerMetadata?.iconColor"
   127→    :on-back="() => router.back()"
   128→  >
   129→    <ProviderSettingsContainer>
   130→      <ProviderBasicSettings
   131→        :title="t('settings.pages.providers.common.section.basic.title')"
   132→        :description="t('settings.pages.providers.common.section.basic.description')"
   133→        :on-reset="handleResetSettings"
   134→      >
   135→        <ProviderBaseUrlInput
   136→          v-model="baseUrl"
   137→          placeholder="http://localhost:11434/v1/"
   138→        />
   139→      </ProviderBasicSettings>
   140→
   141→      <ProviderAdvancedSettings :title="t('settings.pages.providers.common.section.advanced.title')">
   142→        <FieldKeyValues

   144→          :label="t('settings.pages.providers.common.section.advanced.fields.field.headers.label')"
   145→          :description="t('settings.pages.providers.common.section.advanced.fields.field.headers.description')"

   147→          :value-placeholder="t('settings.pages.providers.common.section.advanced.fields.field.headers.value.placeholder')"
   148→          @add="(key: string, value: string) => addKeyValue(headers, key, value)"
   149→          @remove="(index: number) => removeKeyValue(index, headers)"
   150→        />
   151→      </ProviderAdvancedSettings>

# PR Summary: OpenClaw Gateway Provider

## PR Description

This pull request adds OpenClaw as a new LLM provider to the stage-ui package. The implementation enables connections to self-hosted OpenClaw gateways via their OpenAI-compatible chat completions API.

**Key features:**
- Configurable gateway URL (defaults to `http://localhost:3000/v1`)
- Optional bearer token authentication
- Validation checks for connectivity and chat completions support
- Locale entries added for 9 supported languages

## Changed Files

The PR modifies files in `packages/stage-ui/src/libs/providers/`, specifically:
- New OpenClaw provider implementation directory
- Provider index registration updates
- Locale configuration files

## Code Approach

The implementation reuses existing `createOpenAI()` functionality from `@xsai-ext/providers/create` since OpenClaw exposes an OpenAI-compatible API. This design choice avoids code duplication.

Validation deliberately skips model listing because the gateway routes by agent ID rather than maintaining a traditional model catalog—a practical adaptation to OpenClaw's architecture.

## Test Recommendations

The author suggests: verifying the provider appears in Settings → Providers, testing configuration with a running local gateway, and confirming chat message streaming works correctly.

## Files Modified


### 11. **packages/stage-ui/src/libs/providers/providers/openclaw/index.ts** (New file, +51 lines)
```typescript
import { createOpenAI } from '@xsai-ext/providers/create'
import { z } from 'zod'
import { createOpenAICompatibleValidators } from '../../validators/openai-compatible'
import { defineProvider } from '../registry'

const openClawConfigSchema = z.object({
  apiKey: z.string('Auth Token').optional(),
  baseUrl: z.string('Gateway URL').optional().default('http://localhost:3000/v1'),
})

type OpenClawConfig = z.input<typeof openClawConfigSchema>

export const providerOpenClaw = defineProvider<OpenClawConfig>({
  id: 'openclaw',
  name: 'OpenClaw',
  nameLocalize: ({ t }) => t('settings.pages.providers.provider.openclaw.title'),
  description: 'Self-hosted OpenClaw gateway (OpenAI-compatible).',
  descriptionLocalize: ({ t }) => t('settings.pages.providers.provider.openclaw.description'),
  tasks: ['chat'],
  icon: 'i-ph:plugs-connected',
  createProviderConfig: ({ t }) => openClawConfigSchema.extend({
    apiKey: openClawConfigSchema.shape.apiKey.meta({
      labelLocalized: t('settings.pages.providers.catalog.edit.config.common.fields.field.api-key.label'),
      descriptionLocalized: t('settings.pages.providers.catalog.edit.config.common.fields.field.api-key.description'),
      placeholderLocalized: t('settings.pages.providers.catalog.edit.config.common.fields.field.api-key.placeholder'),
      type: 'password',
    }),
    baseUrl: openClawConfigSchema.shape.baseUrl.meta({
      labelLocalized: t('settings.pages.providers.catalog.edit.config.common.fields.field.base-url.label'),
      descriptionLocalized: t('settings.pages.providers.catalog.edit.config.common.fields.field.base-url.description'),
      placeholderLocalized: t('settings.pages.providers.catalog.edit.config.common.fields.field.base-url.placeholder'),
    }),
  }),
  createProvider(config) {
    return createOpenAI(config.apiKey || '', config.baseUrl)
  },
  validationRequiredWhen: () => true,
  validators: {
    ...createOpenAICompatibleValidators({ checks: ['connectivity', 'chat_completions'] }),
  },
})
```

**Summary:** This PR implements OpenClaw provider support with multi-language localization, configuration schema validation, and OpenAI-compatible endpoint handling with optional authentication and custom base URL configuration.

OpenClaw doesn't set this. - The `createProvider` function passes `config.apiKey || ''` whereas openai-compatible passes `config.apiKey as string`. The validation approach here makes sense since OpenClaw has baseUrl as optional with a default value, so it should always be reachable regardless of whether an auth token is provided. 2. **Is there a settings page?** - No `openclaw.vue` file was added in `packages/stage-pages/src/pages` - Ollama and LM Studio have custom settings pages for their provider-specific fields like baseUrl, and OpenClaw needs the same since it has both apiKey and baseUrl to configure. - There's a generic `[providerId].vue` fallback page that might handle this, but I should verify it covers all the necessary fields. 3. **Are there tests?** - No tests were added for OpenClaw. 4. **i18n translations** - The PR adds `title` and `description` to 9 locale files, but I need to check whether the non-English translations are actually translated or just duplicated from English. - Missing troubleshooting validator messages that other providers like Ollama have. 5. **Type definitions and exports** - `OpenClawConfig` is defined but not exported from the module. - The provider itself isn't exported from the index, though this seems consistent with how other providers are handled. 6. **Validation concerns** - The `validationRequiredWhen: () => true` setting means validation always runs regardless of whether baseUrl is actually configured, which could trigger false failures. - The validators only check for connectivity without covering other potential issues. - Missing the `business` property that provides troubleshooting context in other providers. - No `order` property for UI sorting like other providers have. Now I understand the structure. The i18n key for provider names/descriptions in the onboarding/card UI are under `settings.pages.providers.provider.{provider-id}.title/description`. But the PR's code uses `t('settings.pages.providers.provider.openclaw.title')` and `t('settings.pages.providers.provider.openclaw.description')`. Looking at the actual YAML path in the file, the provider entries under the providers section look like: ```yaml settings: pages: providers: provider: ollama: title: Ollama description: ollama.ai ``` But the PR is adding the same English text as the content for all locales instead of providing actual translations—that's a significant problem since these keys are being added to Spanish, French, Japanese, Korean, Russian, Vietnamese, and Chinese locales without any localization. The provider code references `t('settings.pages.providers.provider.openclaw.title')` and `t('settings.pages.providers.provider.openclaw.description')`, so I need to verify these paths match the YAML structure. Looking at the en/settings.yaml file, I can see `openclaw` should sit between `comet-api` and `cerebras` under the `settings.pages.providers.provider` path, which means the YAML keys are correctly positioned in the hierarchy. ``` yaml comet-api: description: CometAPI.com title: Comet API openclaw: description: Self-hosted OpenClaw gateway (OpenAI-compatible) title: OpenClaw cerebras: description: cerebras.ai title: Cerebras ``` Now I'm checking the `[providerId].vue` page to see if a custom settings page is needed. I'm noticing a few issues with the configuration: the `order` property is missing (every other provider has one), there's no `business` property for additional info like Ollama has, and the validation is set to always run even when nothing's configured yet. Since OpenClaw has a default URL like Ollama does, this might work, but the optional API key could cause validation failures. I also don't see a corresponding settings page file in the stage-pages directory. /settings/providers/chat/openclaw.vue` was added - The generic `[providerId].vue` should handle providers with standard fields, but let me check if that handles both apiKey and baseUrl 3. **Missing tests:** - No tests were added for the OpenClaw provider - The existing test file only tests openai-compatible 4. **i18n translations:** - Non-English locales have English text copied (not translated) - Missing troubleshooting/business-related i18n keys (though these would only matter if the business property was added) 5. **Type definitions:** - `OpenClawConfig` type is defined but not exported (may or may not matter based on how other providers handle this) 6. **OpenClaw-specific handling:** - No `model_list` validation - intentionally skipped - Validation always triggers even without an auth token, and the provider creation passes an empty string for the API key if one isn't provided Now I need to check the generic provider settings component to see whether it properly handles both the API key and base URL fields.

ASSISTANTMESSAGE #88
Now I have all the information I need to write a comprehensive review. Let me summarize my findings: **1. Pattern adherence:** - ✅ Uses `defineProvider`, `createOpenAI`, `createOpenAICompatibleValidators`, `z.object`, same schema pattern - ❌ Missing `order` property — all "top" providers (openai, ollama, openai-compatible, deepseek, anthropic, google-generative-ai, 302-ai, openrouter, n1n) have an explicit `order`. Other providers (groq, featherless, comet-api, etc.) don't have one either. So this is acceptable but worth noting. - ❌ The validation logic is problematic — setting `validationRequiredWhen: () => true` means validation always runs, but since the auth token is optional and baseUrl defaults to `localhost:3000`, users without OpenClaw set up will constantly see validation errors. It should check whether the baseUrl is actually configured or non-empty, similar to how groq validates only when an API key is present. - ❌ The provider creation is inconsistent — passing `config.apiKey || ''` as an empty string when auth is missing could cause authentication failures on the gateway, and if `config.baseUrl` is undefined, it won't fall back to the default properly. - ❌ Missing the `business` property with troubleshooting content that ollama includes, and no `iconColor` property (though these aren't universal across providers). - ✅ The icon choice is acceptable even though it's not from lobe-icons. - ❌ No dedicated settings page for OpenClaw, though the generic provider settings page would handle both `apiKey` and `baseUrl` fields at the expected route. - The generic page uses a misleading `sk-...` placeholder for API keys, which doesn't fit a gateway bearer token — a custom page would be cleaner. - I'm noticing that ollama has both a custom settings page and lives in the providers folder, while lm-studio has a custom page but isn't in the providers directory. This suggests custom pages are created when providers need UI beyond the generic template. For OpenClaw, the generic page would suffice unless there's a specific reason to customize it further. - Actually, the key issue is that `baseUrl` sits in the Advanced section of the generic page, but for a local gateway like OpenClaw, users might expect the gateway URL to be more prominent in the Basic section — that's a legitimate reason to build a dedicated settings page. - Tests are missing for the OpenClaw provider, though the existing test suite covers the store adequately. Adding a test for `addProvider('openclaw')` and `removeProvider` would align with the existing patterns, but it's not a blocker. - The i18n translations are a real problem: all nine locales have English text for the description. While the brand name "OpenClaw" can stay the same across locales, the description "Self-hosted OpenClaw gateway (OpenAI-compatible)" should be translated. Other providers like `openai-compatible` have proper Japanese translations, so this is inconsistent. - The `OpenClawConfig` type isn't exported, which matches the pattern for other providers like `GroqConfig`, so that's fine. - The gateway URL defaults correctly to `http://localhost:3000/v1` and the optional auth token is there, but `validationRequiredWhen: () => true` means it validates even without any configuration, which seems like an odd policy choice. - Skipping the `model_list` check is intentional per the PR (the gateway routes by agent ID), but this should really be documented in a code comment. - There's no dedicated `validateConfig` validator like ollama and cloudflare have, so if the baseUrl is malformed, users just get a cryptic connectivity error instead of a clear validation message. - The biggest gap is the missing dedicated settings page for OpenClaw — the generic page works but buries the gateway URL in Advanced and the API key placeholder text isn't specific to this provider. - All 9 non-English locale files still have English text instead of proper translations. - The `validationRequiredWhen: () => true` setup means it'll always try connecting to localhost:3000, which causes errors for users who haven't actually set up the provider yet. - Missing an `order` property for consistency with other top-tier providers. - No test coverage added for the OpenClaw provider in the store test file, which breaks the pattern of testing provider add/remove operations. - The `createProvider` call is passing `config.api` but the implementation appears incomplete. - If the gateway requires authentication, passing an empty string as the Bearer token won't work—it should either pass `undefined` or include conditional logic. - Using a generic icon instead of a lobe-icons icon is inconsistent with the rest of the provider catalog. Now I'm realizing I need to post this review as a GitHub comment, but I don't have access to a Bash tool to run the `gh pr review` command. Let me check what tools are actually available to me. Looking at my available tools—Glob, Grep, Read, WebFetch, WebSearch—none of them are Bash. I could potentially use the GitHub API directly through WebFetch to post the review, but I should first let the user know that I can't execute the gh CLI command directly and offer to provide the review text for them to post instead.

ASSISTANTMESSAGE #89
Now I have enough information for a comprehensive review. I don't have a Bash tool to run `gh pr review` directly, so I'll provide the complete review text for you and also note this limitation. Here's my full analysis of PR #1: --- ## Review Findings ### 1. Provider Pattern (`packages/stage-ui/src/libs/providers/providers/openclaw/index.ts`) **Inconsistencies vs. existing providers:** - **`validationRequiredWhen: () => true`** — This always fires the connectivity check, even if the user hasn't configured anything. Every other provider with an optional API key (groq, featherless, comet-api, openai-compatible) uses `validationRequiredWhen(config) { return !!config.apiKey?.trim() }`. Since the auth token is optional for OpenClaw, users who haven't set it up will constantly see connectivity failures to `localhost:3000`. Ollama uses `() => true` but that's intentional for a local-first provider where the server is always expected to be running — OpenClaw's auth token being optional makes this different. - **`createProvider` uses `config.apiKey || ''`** — If the gateway requires auth, an empty string gets sent as a Bearer token. Should be `createOpenAI(config.apiKey as string, config.baseUrl)` (matching how other providers handle optional keys) or pass `undefined` when empty. - **Missing `order` property** — Providers that are prominently featured (openai, ollama, openai-compatible, deepseek, anthropic, google-generative-ai, etc.) all set an explicit `order`. Without it, OpenClaw gets `order: 99999` from the registry default and floats to the bottom of the list. This may be intentional but should be explicit. - **No `validateConfig` validator** — Ollama validates that `baseUrl` is a non-empty, valid absolute URL before attempting connectivity. OpenClaw skips this, so a malformed URL will produce a cryptic connectivity error rather than a clear "invalid URL" message. - **No `business` property** — Ollama adds troubleshooting content via `business: ({ t }) => (...)`. Not universal (most providers skip it), but for a local gateway with common setup errors, this would be valuable. - **Generic icon** — `i-ph:plugs-connected` works but is not an lobe-icons branded icon. Other providers use `i-lobe-icons:*`. Not a blocker, but worth noting if an icon is available. ### 2. Missing Settings Page **File needed:** `packages/stage-pages/src/pages/settings/providers/chat/openclaw.vue` The generic `[providerId].vue` will catch `openclaw` and render both fields, but with two problems: 1. The gateway URL (`baseUrl`) is placed in the **Advanced** section — for a local self-hosted gateway, this is a primary config field and should be in the Basic section. 2. The API key placeholder shows `sk-...`, which is misleading for a bearer auth token. Ollama and LM Studio both have dedicated pages for exactly this reason. OpenClaw needs one too, similar to `lm-studio.vue` but with both `apiKey` and `baseUrl` in the Basic section. ### 3. Missing Tests No tests were added. `packages/stage-ui/src/stores/provider-catalog.test.ts` has `add` and `remove` tests using `providerOpenAICompatible`. A parallel test for OpenClaw would be: ```ts import { providerOpenClaw } from '../libs/providers/providers/openclaw' it('add openclaw', () => { const store = useProviderCatalogStore() store.addProvider(providerOpenClaw.id) expect(Object.values(store.configs)[0].definitionId).toBe('openclaw') expect(Object.values(store.configs)[0].name).toBe('OpenClaw') }) ``` ### 4. i18n — Non-English Translations Are Not Translated The PR adds `openclaw.title` and `openclaw.description` to all 9 locale files, but the content in `es`, `fr`, `ja`, `ko`, `ru`, `vi`, `zh-Hans`, and `zh-Hant` is the same English text as `en`. Looking at existing locale files, other providers localize their descriptions (e.g., `ja/settings.yaml` has `openai-compatible: description: OpenAI互換`). At minimum the non-English descriptions should be translated or flagged as needing translation (with a TODO comment). Additionally, the provider definition also references i18n keys used by ollama's `business` troubleshooting section — if troubleshooting content is added in future, the locale keys will need to be added too. ### 5. Type Definitions and Exports - `OpenClawConfig` is defined but not exported — consistent with other providers (GroqConfig, FeatherlessConfig also unexported). No issue here. - The `import './openclaw'` line added to `packages/stage-ui/src/libs/providers/providers/index.ts` is correct. - No missing exports. ### 6. OpenClaw-Specific Behavior - **Gateway URL**: Default `http://localhost:3000/v1` is reasonable. ✅ - **Auth token**: Optional, passed via `createOpenAI` Bearer header. ✅ - **Model listing skipped**: The PR description explains this is intentional because OpenClaw routes by agent ID, not model names. This is valid, but should have a code comment explaining why `model_list` is excluded, otherwise future reviewers will wonder if it's an oversight. - **Validator spread**: `...createOpenAICompatibleValidators({ checks: ['connectivity', 'chat_completions'] })` — note that validators for `openai-compatible` use `checks: ['connectivity', 'model_list', 'chat_completions']` and ollama uses the same. Omitting `model_list` is fine but deserves a comment. --- **Summary of required changes:** | # | File | Issue | |---|------|-------| | 1 | `providers/openclaw/index.ts` | Fix `validationRequiredWhen` — should only validate when baseUrl is non-default or apiKey is set | | 2 | `providers/openclaw/index.ts` | Add a comment explaining why `model_list` check is excluded | | 3 | `providers/openclaw/index.ts` | Add `validateConfig` to check baseUrl is a valid URL | | 4 | `pages/settings/providers/chat/openclaw.vue` | **Create this file** — a dedicated settings page with gateway URL in Basic section | | 5 | `stores/provider-catalog.test.ts` | Add add/remove tests for openclaw | | 6 | `i18n/src/locales/*/settings.yaml` | Actually translate the `description` in non-English locales (or mark TODO) | I wasn't able to post this directly via `gh pr review` because no Bash/shell tool is available in this environment. You can run the following to post it: ```sh gh pr review 1 --comment --body "$(cat <<'EOF' ## Code Review: OpenClaw Gateway Provider ### 1.     "text": "Now I have enough information for a comprehensive review. I don't have a Bash tool to run `gh pr review` directly, so I'll provide the complete review text for you and also note this limitation.\n\nHere's my full analysis of PR #1:\n\n---\n\n## Review Findings\n\n### 1. Provider Pattern (`packages/stage-ui/src/libs/providers/providers/openclaw/index.ts`)\n\n**Inconsistencies vs. existing providers:**\n\n- **`validationRequiredWhen: () => true`** \u2014 This always fires the connectivity check, even if the user hasn't configured anything. Every other provider with an optional API key (groq, featherless, comet-api, openai-compatible) uses `validationRequiredWhen(config) { return !!config.apiKey?.trim() }`. Since the auth token is optional for OpenClaw, users who haven't set it up will constantly see connectivity failures to `localhost:3000`. Ollama uses `() => true` but that's intentional for a local-first provider where the server is always expected to be running \u2014 OpenClaw's auth token being optional makes this different.\n\n- **`createProvider` uses `config.apiKey || ''`** \u2014 If the gateway requires auth, an empty string gets sent as a Bearer token. Should be `createOpenAI(config.apiKey as string, config.baseUrl)` (matching how other providers handle optional keys) or pass `undefined` when empty.\n\n- **Missing `order` property** \u2014 Providers that are prominently featured (openai, ollama, openai-compatible, deepseek, anthropic, google-generative-ai, etc.) all set an explicit `order`. Without it, OpenClaw gets `order: 99999` from the registry default and floats to the bottom of the list. This may be intentional but should be explicit.\n\n- **No `validateConfig` validator** \u2014 Ollama validates that `baseUrl` is a non-empty, valid absolute URL before attempting connectivity. OpenClaw skips this, so a malformed URL will produce a cryptic connectivity error rather than a clear \"invalid URL\" message.\n\n- **No `business` property** \u2014 Ollama adds troubleshooting content via `business: ({ t }) => (...)`. Not universal (most providers skip it), but for a local gateway with common setup errors, this would be valuable.\n\n- **Generic icon** \u2014 `i-ph:plugs-connected` works but is not an lobe-icons branded icon. Other providers use `i-lobe-icons:*`. Not a blocker, but worth noting if an icon is available.\n\n### 2. Missing Settings Page\n\n**File needed:** `packages/stage-pages/src/pages/settings/providers/chat/openclaw.vue`\n\nThe generic `[providerId].vue` will catch `openclaw` and render both fields, but with two problems:\n1. The gateway URL (`baseUrl`) is placed in the **Advanced** section \u2014 for a local self-hosted gateway, this is a primary config field and should be in the Basic section.\n2. The API key placeholder shows `sk-...`, which is misleading for a bearer auth token.\n\nOllama and LM Studio both have dedicated pages for exactly this reason. OpenClaw needs one too, similar to `lm-studio.vue` but with both `apiKey` and `baseUrl` in the Basic section.\n\n### 3. Missing Tests\n\nNo tests were added. `packages/stage-ui/src/stores/provider-catalog.test.ts` has `add` and `remove` tests using `providerOpenAICompatible`. A parallel test for OpenClaw would be:\n\n```ts\nimport { providerOpenClaw } from '../libs/providers/providers/openclaw'\n\nit('add openclaw', () => {\n  const store = useProviderCatalogStore()\n  store.addProvider(providerOpenClaw.id)\n  expect(Object.values(store.configs)[0].definitionId).toBe('openclaw')\n  expect(Object.values(store.configs)[0].name).toBe('OpenClaw')\n})\n```\n\n### 4. i18n \u2014 Non-English Translations Are Not Translated\n\nThe PR adds `openclaw.title` and `openclaw.description` to all 9 locale files, but the content in `es`, `fr`, `ja`, `ko`, `ru`, `vi`, `zh-Hans`, and `zh-Hant` is the same English text as `en`. Looking at existing locale files, other providers localize their descriptions (e.g., `ja/settings.yaml` has `openai-compatible: description: OpenAI\u4e92\u63db`). At minimum the non-English descriptions should be translated or flagged as needing translation (with a TODO comment).\n\nAdditionally, the provider definition also references i18n keys used by ollama's `business` troubleshooting section \u2014 if troubleshooting content is added in future, the locale keys will need to be added too.\n\n### 5. Type Definitions and Exports\n\n- `OpenClawConfig` is defined but not exported \u2014 consistent with other providers (GroqConfig, FeatherlessConfig also unexported). No issue here.\n- The `import './openclaw'` line added to `packages/stage-ui/src/libs/providers/providers/index.ts` is correct.\n- No missing exports.\n\n### 6. OpenClaw-Specific Behavior\n\n- **Gateway URL**: Default `http://localhost:3000/v1` is reasonable. \u2705\n- **Auth token**: Optional, passed via `createOpenAI` Bearer header. \u2705  \n- **Model listing skipped**: The PR description explains this is intentional because OpenClaw routes by agent ID, not model names. This is valid, but should have a code comment explaining why `model_list` is excluded, otherwise future reviewers will wonder if it's an oversight.\n- **Validator spread**: `...createOpenAICompatibleValidators({ checks: ['connectivity', 'chat_completions'] })` \u2014 note that validators for `openai-compatible` use `checks: ['connectivity', 'model_list', 'chat_completions']` and ollama uses the same. Omitting `model_list` is fine but deserves a comment.\n\n---\n\n**Summary of required changes:**\n\n| # | File | Issue |\n|---|------|-------|\n| 1 | `providers/openclaw/index.ts` | Fix `validationRequiredWhen` \u2014 should only validate when baseUrl is non-default or apiKey is set |\n| 2 | `providers/openclaw/index.ts` | Add a comment explaining why `model_list` check is excluded |\n| 3 | `providers/openclaw/index.ts` | Add `validateConfig` to check baseUrl is a valid URL |\n| 4 | `pages/settings/providers/chat/openclaw.vue` | **Create this file** \u2014 a dedicated settings page with gateway URL in Basic section |\n| 5 | `stores/provider-catalog.test.ts` | Add add/remove tests for openclaw |\n| 6 | `i18n/src/locales/*/settings.yaml` | Actually translate the `description` in non-English locales (or mark TODO) |\n\nI wasn't able to post this directly via `gh pr review` because no Bash/shell tool is available in this environment. You can run the following to post it:\n\n```sh\ngh pr review 1 --comment --body \"$(cat <<'EOF'\n## Code Review: OpenClaw Gateway Provider\n\n### 1.
